#### Image pre-processing

The image pre-processing works in the same way as was presented during lectures:
* Convert to grayscale
* Apply Canny Edge detector
* Cut region of interested

#### Finding Lines in single frame
* Lines are detected using `cv2.HoughLinesP()`.
* For each detected line slope is calculated.
* Lines are removed if corresponding slope is outside defined range
* Detected lines are split into different sets. One set for left lines and the
other for right line. This I can detect from the slope (negative or positive)

Hopefully selected lines do belong to the right or left line.
Finally I take only points from each line and use [Polynomial
regression](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Polynomial_regression) to find
coefficients $$y=a+bx$$
And that is enough to draw the line.

#### Remarks
The weak part is that I only use 1-degree polynomial, yielding to the line
regression, thus curved lines aren't fitted nicely (optional video). Also,
proper stabilisation mechanism is required to avoid "line jumpings". This could
probably be achieved using [confidence
bands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confidence_and_prediction_bands) and if
detected lines doesn't nicely fit in the expected range then use previously
detected line, allowing smooth transitions. <br/>
Further improvemtents could be made by slicing frame into smaller regions and
try to detect lane in each region. <br/>
Optional solution performace at the moment isn't good and further investigation
is required. <br/>
Other weak part is that code needs to be refactored, since most of the stuff are
added to collect data for analysis.<br/>

```{.python .input  n=1}
#importing some useful packages
import matplotlib.pyplot as plt
import matplotlib.image as mpimg
import numpy as np
import cv2
import math
import numpy.polynomial.polynomial as poly
import os
from moviepy.editor import VideoFileClip
from IPython.display import HTML

%matplotlib inline
```

```{.python .input  n=2}
def calc_slope(x1, y1, x2, y2):
    return ((y2-y1)/(x2-x1))

def weighted_img(image1, image2, α=0.8, β=1., λ=0.):
    return cv2.addWeighted(image1, α, image2, β, λ)

```

```{.python .input  n=3}
class Settings(object):
    def __init__(self, 
                 kernel_size=3, 
                 low_threshold=50, 
                 high_threshold=150, 
                 rho=2, 
                 theta=np.pi/180, 
                 threshold=15, 
                 min_line_len=20, 
                 max_line_gap=10,
                 relative_region = [(1, 1), (0.49, 0.60), (0.535, 0.60), (1, 1)],
                 slope_filtering = True,
                 crop_middle_road = False
                ):
        self.kernel_size = kernel_size
        self.low_threshold=low_threshold
        self.high_threshold = high_threshold
        self.rho = rho
        self.theta = theta
        self.threshold = threshold
        self.min_line_len = min_line_len
        self.max_line_gap = max_line_gap
        self.relative_region = np.array(relative_region)
        self.crop_middle_road = crop_middle_road
        #[0.55;0.7] and [−0.96;−0.61]
        #self.slope_valid_range = (-0.5, -0.8, 0.5, 0.8)
        self.slope_valid_range = (-0.61, -0.96, 0.55, 0.7)
        self.slope_filtering = slope_filtering
        
    def region(self, image):
        imshape = image.shape
        ysize = imshape[0]
        xsize = imshape[1]
        
        return np.array([[
                    (0*self.relative_region[0,0], ysize*self.relative_region[0,1]),
                    (xsize*self.relative_region[1,0], ysize*self.relative_region[1,1]),
                    (xsize*self.relative_region[2,0], ysize*self.relative_region[2,1]),
                    (xsize*self.relative_region[3,0], ysize*self.relative_region[3,1]),
                ]], dtype='int')
```

```{.python .input  n=4}
# Helpful methods to work with image simply to separate line detection logic with
# image related methods
class Frame(object):
    def __init__(self, image, settings = None, initial_image = None):
        if settings is None:
            self.settings = Settings()
        else:
            self.settings = settings
        self.image = image
        self.initial_image = initial_image
    
    def apply_grayscale(self):
        self.image = cv2.cvtColor(self.image, cv2.COLOR_BGR2GRAY)
        return self
        
    def apply_Canny(self):
        self.image = cv2.Canny(
            self.image, 
            self.settings.low_threshold, 
            self.settings.high_threshold
        )
        return self
    
    def apply_gaussian_blur(self):
        s = self.settings
        self.image = cv2.GaussianBlur(self.image, (s.kernel_size, s.kernel_size), 0)
        return self
        
    def cut_region_of_interest(self):
        """
        Applies an image mask.
    
        Only keeps the region of the image defined by the polygon
        formed from `vertices`. The rest of the image is set to black.
        """
        
        img = self.image
        vertices = self.settings.region(img)
        
        #defining a blank mask to start with
        mask = np.zeros_like(img)   
    
        #defining a 3 channel or 1 channel color to fill the mask with depending on the input image
        if len(img.shape) > 2:
            channel_count = img.shape[2]  # i.e. 3 or 4 depending on your image
            ignore_mask_color = (255,) * channel_count
        else:
            ignore_mask_color = 255
        
        #filling pixels inside the polygon defined by "vertices" with the fill color    
        cv2.fillPoly(mask, vertices, ignore_mask_color)

        
    
        #returning the image only where mask pixels are nonzero
        masked_image = cv2.bitwise_and(img, mask)
        self.image = masked_image

        # Remove middle of the road, just to improve detection on optional video
        if self.settings.crop_middle_road == True:
            ysize = img.shape[0]
            xsize = img.shape[1]

            v = np.array([
                ((xsize/2 - 250, ysize), (xsize/2+370, ysize),
                (xsize/2, ysize/2+120), (xsize/2+50, ysize/2+120))
            ], dtype='int')

            cv2.fillPoly(self.image, v, color=[0,0,0])
        
        return self        
```

```{.python .input  n=5}
# Here goes main logic to detect lane
class LaneDetector(object):
    '''
    extract_line - just calls hough lines and returns list of lines
    split_lanes - Takes all lines and sorts them into left/right sets based on the slope
    extract_points - Iterates over all lines and returns list of points
    fit_lanes - Applies pollyfit to the points
    calc_lane_lines - Using coefficents which we get from fit_lanes calculate left/right lines
    '''
    def __init__(self, frame, settings=None):
        if settings is None:
            self.settings = Settings()
        else:
            self.settings = settings
        self.frame = frame
        self.region = (
            frame.apply_grayscale()
                 .apply_gaussian_blur()
                 .apply_Canny()
                 .cut_region_of_interest()
                 .image
        )
        self.valid = False
    
    def extract_lines(self):
        s = self.settings
        self.lines = cv2.HoughLinesP(
            self.region, 
            s.rho, s.theta, s.threshold, np.array([]), 
            minLineLength=s.min_line_len, maxLineGap=s.max_line_gap
        )
        return self
    
    def fit_lanes(self):
        def fit(points):
            x = points[0:,0]
            y = points[0:,1]
            coeffs = poly.polyfit(x, y, 1)
            return coeffs
        
        if len(self.left_lane_points) > 0 and len(self.right_lane_points):
            self.left_lane_coeffs = fit(self.left_lane_points)
            self.right_lane_coeffs = fit(self.right_lane_points)
        else:
            self.left_lane_coeffs = None
            self.right_lane_coeffs = None
        return self
        
    def calc_lane_lines(self):
        img_x = self.region.shape[1]
        img_y = self.region.shape[0]
        
        self.fit_lanes()
        def calc_line(coeffs, reg_y):
            c,b = coeffs
            y1 = img_y*reg_y
            y2 = img_y
            
            lx1 = int(round((y2-c)/b))
            lx2 = int(round((y1-c)/b))
        
            lp1 = (lx1, int(y2))
            lp2 = (lx2, int(y1))
            
            return (lp1, lp2)
            
        if self.left_lane_coeffs is not None and self.right_lane_coeffs is not None:
            reg_y1 = self.settings.relative_region[1,1]
            reg_y2 = self.settings.relative_region[2,1]
            self.left_lane = calc_line(self.left_lane_coeffs, reg_y1)
            self.right_lane = calc_line(self.right_lane_coeffs, reg_y2)
            self.valid = True
        else:
            self.left_lane = None
            self.right_lane = None
            self.valid = False
        
        return self
            
    def split_lanes(self):
        lines = self.extract_lines()
        slope_range = self.settings.slope_valid_range
        
        self.left_lane_lines = []
        self.right_lane_lines = []
        for line in self.lines:
            for x1,y1,x2,y2 in line:
                slope = calc_slope(x1,y1,x2,y2)

                # slope filtering is true then only take lines which slope is between 
                # defined range to get rid of lines which might be wrongly detected
                if slope < 0.0:
                    if self.settings.slope_filtering is True:
                        if slope_range[1] < slope < slope_range[0]:
                            self.right_lane_lines.append(line)
                    else:
                        self.right_lane_lines.append(line)
                else:
                    if self.settings.slope_filtering is True:
                        if slope_range[2] < slope < slope_range[3]:
                            self.left_lane_lines.append(line)
                    else:
                        self.left_lane_lines.append(line)
        
        self.right_lane_lines = np.array(self.right_lane_lines)
        self.left_lane_lines = np.array(self.left_lane_lines)
        return self
    
    def extract_points(self):
        
        self.split_lanes()
        self.left_lane_points = []
        self.right_lane_points = []
        
        def iterate(lines):
            points = []
            for line in lines:
                for x1,y1,x2,y2 in line:
                    points.append((x1,y1))
                    points.append((x2,y2))
            return np.array(points)
        
        self.left_lane_points = iterate(self.left_lane_lines)
        self.right_lane_points = iterate(self.right_lane_lines)
        return self
    
```

```{.python .input  n=6}
# Helper class just to draw lines on top of the image
class LaneDecorator(object):
    def __init__(self, image=None, detector=None):
        self.image = image
        self.decorated_img = np.zeros((*image.shape, 3), dtype=np.uint8)
        
    def draw_lines(self, lines, color=[255,0,0,0], thickness=3):
        for line in lines:
            for x1,y1,x2,y2 in line:
                cv2.line(self.decorated_img, (x1, y1), (x2, y2), color, thickness) 
    
    def draw_points(self, points, color=[255,0,0], thickness=3):
        for x1, y1 in points:
            # TODO: change to normal points
            cv2.circle(self.decorated_img, (x1,y1), 3, color, thickness)
    
    def draw_lane(self, lane, color=[255,0,0], thickness=2):
        if lane is not None:
            cv2.line(self.decorated_img, lane[0], lane[1], color, thickness)
    
    def draw_lanes(self, lanes, color=[255,0,0], thickness=3):
        for lane in lanes:
            self.draw_lane(lane, color, thickness)
            
```

```{.python .input  n=7}
# First lets try to see how well lines and points are detected 

img_files = os.listdir("test_images/")
image = mpimg.imread('test_images/{0}'.format(img_files[2]))
frame = Frame(image)

lane_detector = LaneDetector(frame)
lane_detector.split_lanes()
lane_detector.extract_points()
lane_detector.calc_lane_lines()

decorator = LaneDecorator(frame.image)
decorator.draw_lines(lane_detector.right_lane_lines, [0,255,0])
decorator.draw_lines(lane_detector.left_lane_lines, [255,0,0])
decorator.draw_points(lane_detector.left_lane_points, color=[255,255, 255], thickness=5)
decorator.draw_points(lane_detector.right_lane_points, color=[255,255,255])

plt.imshow(decorator.image, cmap='gray')

```

```{.python .input  n=8}
# try to paint it on the image
image = mpimg.imread('test_images/{0}'.format(img_files[2]))
frame = Frame(image)

lane_detector = LaneDetector(frame)
lane_detector.split_lanes()
lane_detector.extract_points()
lane_detector.calc_lane_lines()

decorator = LaneDecorator(frame.image)
decorator.draw_lane(lane_detector.left_lane, color=[0,255,0], thickness=15)
decorator.draw_lane(lane_detector.right_lane, color=[0,0,255], thickness=15)

img = weighted_img(image, decorator.decorated_img)

plt.imshow(img)

```

```{.python .input  n=9}
left_coeff_list = []
right_coeff_list = []
left_lines = None
right_lines = None
fitted_left_lanes = None
fitted_right_lanes = None
v_frame = None

def processor(settings = None):
    '''
    processor() returns function which is passed to fl_image to do all video processing
    also tracks some extra information for analysis
    '''
    global left_coeff_list
    global right_coeff_list
    global left_lines
    global right_lines
    global fitted_left_lanes
    global fitted_right_lanes
    global v_frame
    
    fitted_left_lanes = []
    fitted_right_lanes = []

    left_lines = None
    right_lines = None
    
    left_coeff_list = []
    right_coeff_list = []
    
    if settings is None:
        settings = Settings()
    left_fallback = None
    right_fallback = None
    v_frame = None
    
    def process_image(im):
            global left_fallback
            global right_fallback
            global left_lines
            global right_lines
            global v_frame
            
            frame = Frame(im, settings=settings)
            v_frame = frame
            lane_detector = LaneDetector(frame, settings=settings)
            lane_detector.split_lanes()
            lane_detector.extract_points()
            lane_detector.calc_lane_lines()
            
            if len(lane_detector.left_lane_lines) > 0:
                if left_lines is None:
                    left_lines = lane_detector.left_lane_lines
                else:
                    left_lines = np.vstack([left_lines, lane_detector.left_lane_lines])
            
            if len(lane_detector.right_lane_lines) > 0:
                if right_lines is None:
                    right_lines = lane_detector.right_lane_lines
                else:
                    right_lines = np.vstack([right_lines, lane_detector.right_lane_lines])
            
            if lane_detector.valid is True:
                decorator = LaneDecorator(frame.image)
                c, b = lane_detector.left_lane_coeffs
                
                fitted_left_lanes.append(lane_detector.left_lane)
                decorator.draw_lane(lane_detector.left_lane, color=[255,0,0], thickness=15)
                left_coeff_list.append(b)
                
                c, b = lane_detector.right_lane_coeffs
                fitted_right_lanes.append(lane_detector.right_lane)
                decorator.draw_lane(lane_detector.right_lane, color=[255,0,0], thickness=15)
                right_coeff_list.append(b)
                    
                img = weighted_img(im, decorator.decorated_img)
                return img
            else:
                return im
        
    return process_image
```

```{.python .input  n=10}
white_output = 'white.mp4'
clip1 = VideoFileClip("solidWhiteRight.mp4")
white_clip = clip1.fl_image(processor(settings=Settings(crop_middle_road=False))) #NOTE: this function expects color images!!
%time white_clip.write_videofile(white_output, audio=False)
```

```{.python .input  n=17}
from IPython.display import Latex
```

```{.python .input  n=18}

def calc_slopes(lines):
    slopes = []
    for line in lines:
        for x1,y1,x2,y2 in line:
            slopes.append(calc_slope(x1,y1,x2,y2))
    return np.array(slopes)

```

```{.python .input  n=19}
%%latex
Let
\begin{equation}
\vec{\mathbf{Y}}^T = (L_1, L_2, ..., L_n)
\qquad
L_n=\{(x,y)\mid y=mx+c\}
\qquad
m=\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}.
\end{equation}

\[f(m) = \left\{
  \begin{array}{lr}
    lane_{right} & : m < 0\\
    lane_{left} & : m \ge 0
  \end{array}
\right.
\]
        
Here $L_n$ are observed lines from the video frame.
Let's assume that
        
\begin{equation}
m\ \sim \ {\mathcal {N}}(\mu ,\,\sigma ^{2})
\end{equation}


```

```{.json .output n=19}
[
 {
  "data": {
   "text/latex": "Let\n\\begin{equation}\n\\vec{\\mathbf{Y}}^T = (L_1, L_2, ..., L_n)\n\\qquad\nL_n=\\{(x,y)\\mid y=mx+c\\}\n\\qquad\nm=\\frac{y_2-y_1}{x_2-x_1}.\n\\end{equation}\n\n\\[f(m) = \\left\\{\n  \\begin{array}{lr}\n    lane_{right} & : m < 0\\\\\n    lane_{left} & : m \\ge 0\n  \\end{array}\n\\right.\n\\]\n        \nHere $L_n$ are observed lines from the video frame.\nLet's assume that\n        \n\\begin{equation}\nm\\ \\sim \\ {\\mathcal {N}}(\\mu ,\\,\\sigma ^{2})\n\\end{equation}\n",
   "text/plain": "<IPython.core.display.Latex object>"
  },
  "metadata": {},
  "output_type": "display_data"
 }
]
```

```{.python .input  n=20}
# all detected lines merged into single frame
decorator = LaneDecorator(v_frame.image)
decorator.draw_lines(left_lines, [0,255,0])
decorator.draw_lines(right_lines, [255,0,0])
plt.imshow(decorator.decorated_img, cmap='gray')
```

#### Descriptive statistics

To get rid of incorrectly detected lines it is safe to assume that we should
only consider slopes between $ [0.55;0.7] $ and $ [-0.96;-0.61]$ intervals

### Fitting line

```{.python .input  n=27}
%%latex
General form of lane line
\begin{equation}

{\displaystyle {\begin{bmatrix}
    y_{1}\\y_{2}\\y_{3}\\\vdots \\y_{n}
    \end{bmatrix}}=
 {\begin{bmatrix}1&x_{1}
  \\1&x_{2}
  \\1&x_{3}
  \\\vdots &\vdots 
  \\1&x_{n}\end{bmatrix}}{
    \begin{bmatrix}a_{0}\\a_{1}\\a_{2}\\\vdots \\a_{n}\end{bmatrix}}+{\begin{bmatrix}\varepsilon _{1}\\\varepsilon _{2}\\\varepsilon _{3}\\\vdots \\\varepsilon _{n}\end{bmatrix}},}
\end{equation}
\begin{equation}
\vec y_k = \mathbf{X_k} \vec a_k + \vec\varepsilon. \,
\qquad
\varepsilon\ \sim \ {\mathcal {N}}(\mu ,\,\sigma ^{2})
\qquad
k = 1 \dots frames
\end{equation}

Where $x_n$ are points from detected lines.  
```

```{.json .output n=27}
 }
```

```{.python .input  n=28}
# all fitted lines
decorator = LaneDecorator(v_frame.image)
decorator.draw_lanes(fitted_left_lanes, [0,255,0])
decorator.draw_lanes(fitted_right_lanes, [255,0,0])
plt.imshow(decorator.decorated_img, cmap='gray')
```

#### Further investigation

After removing incorrectly detected lines and fitting line in some cases
calculated slope still makes big jumps. In this case we need to build stabiliser
which would compare fitted line slope with [confidence
bands](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confidence_and_prediction_bands). Since, it
is simple linear regression [Scheffé's
method](https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scheff%C3%A9%27s_method) should work.
_The investigation was made only on single video._
